    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4bd4a061-bb3b-4172-bcfd-a44e57465b8f'

  <span id="freeText7052545088112318506" style="display:none">Neil Josten is out of time. He knew when he came to PSU he wouldn't survive the year, but with his death right around the corner he's got more reasons than ever to live.<br /><br />Befriending the Foxes was inadvisable. Kissing one is unthinkable. Neil should know better than to get involved with anyone this close to the end, but Andrew's never been the easiest person to walk away from. If they both say it doesn't mean anything, maybe Neil won't regret losing it, but the one person Neil can't lie to is himself.<br /><br />He's got promises to keep and a team to get to championships if he can just outrun Riko a little longer, but Riko's not the only monster in Neil's life. The truth might get them all killed—or be Neil's one shot at getting out of this alive.</span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23667559-the-king-s-men">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2304549450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4516063975106700154"><b>read 3 [january 2020]</b><br/>so my yearly reread of ATFG is done and now I'm supposed to be sensible and tackle my actual tbr pile for once. 😪 My heart still clings to this series for found-family and for broken kids learning to love and trust and cling on even though they're drowning. And ngl, the mafia parts were brutal and cold and thrilling. I forgot Andrew only says like 9 words the whole book though and it makes me a little sad.<br/><br/>this series is a mess of characters who have attitudes of black ice an</span>
  <span id="freeText4516063975106700154" style="display:none"><b>read 3 [january 2020]</b><br />so my yearly reread of ATFG is done and now I'm supposed to be sensible and tackle my actual tbr pile for once. 😪 My heart still clings to this series for found-family and for broken kids learning to love and trust and cling on even though they're drowning. And ngl, the mafia parts were brutal and cold and thrilling. I forgot Andrew only says like 9 words the whole book though and it makes me a little sad.<br /><br />this series is a mess of characters who have attitudes of black ice and cut glass, and they make unforgivable decisions and can be problematic and cruel...but they're learning to be better. <i>that's</i> what I ask for in a character arc: growth and bitter fighting for change. these Foxes 😭 Neil. Andrew. My heart.<br /><br /><br /><b>read 2 [february 2019]</b><br />i can't b re a t h e. Honestly this series has just caught my heart and hustled its way in to take a firm place on my favourites of all time list. Yes it's messy and imperfect. But it's flawed in such a raw way and the characters are just loveable wretches...I can't evenvennnn. I love Neil. I love his attitude, his vicious need to cling to love, and the way he and Andrew find some peace within each other, something to fight for when the world has only ever left them bloody.<br /><br />UGH I LOVE IT.<br /><br />((i miss it badly already...is a yearly reread needed now? i think yes))<br /><br /><br />*:·ﾟ✧*:·ﾟ✧<br /><b>Read 1 | February 2018</b><br /><br /><b>Well hi I caN'T BREATHE JUST GIVE ME A MOMENT.</b> I think my heart might explode but IT'S FINE, EVERYTHING IS FINE. (Just kidding it's not fine ajdfkasld it's bloody brilliant.) Look, I like this series. I adore it. It's full of messy broken characters who find people to hold onto and that's just the kind of story that I love every. single. time.<br /><br />(I mean, it's even about sport?!? And I'm as sporty as an upsidedown turtle, BUT YET. Here I am.)<br /><br />** Also full warning but I'm going to name the ship, and it's not <i>really</i> a spoiler, but it might be because it's SO SLOW BURN that it takes 3 books to really happen. So if you don't want to know who Neil ends up with...I warned ya mate.<br /><br /><br /><b>There's way too much to freaking say, so here's a list of things I loved:</b><br />• EVERY FRIKKIN THING<br />• haha okay shh I'll be more specific<br />• so the character development (particularly of Andrew and Neil and Kevin) was so intoxicatingly amazing and I'm a fan<br />• I love how it features mental illness and actually tackles it head on and doesn't romanticise it<br />• It's FUNNY. I laughed out loud so many times<br />• and i squeaked...yeah I don't know who I am now either<br />• it's super long but somehow i wanted every page and more<br />• it gets very dark, like darker than the 2nd book and that's saying something, so get ready to lose your mind<br />• also this author does NOT HOLD BACK so people are going to get hurt<br />• I HURT<br />• I HURT A LOT<br />• Coach Wymack is the ultimate mother and I love him<br />• the team having a sleep over with Neil in the middle to keep him safe probably broke my heart<br />• I even couldn't look away from the game section?!?<br />• tHE ENDING WAS SO TENSE<br />• and the ship omg Andrew and Neil are a gift to this world and nearly made me cry<br />• (also can I say that I'm so so impressed at how much consent was pointed at in this book??? obviously Andrew's PTSD makes it a big deal for him, but the fact that this, basically an NA book full of aggressive mouthy athletes, stopped everything and every. time. waited for consent...it just made me really proud. I wish ALL books would do this. Always)<br />• also every Fox character was precious<br />• and like this is a FAMILY and i love them<br />• also Neil gets so freaking hurt and just -- afjdskladfd<br />• this book<br />• I'm actually devastated it's over that is the only thing<br />• wait till I fall into the fanart on pinterest, you'll never see me again<br /><br /><br /><b> I think it's worth mentioning that this isn't the kind of book where you condone all the characters' actions</b>. They do hella problematic things. Andrew still needs to chill the heck out and some things he does are NOT ok. But, like I said in my review of bk 2: I think these characters are messy and sometimes awful and often times wrong, but I think the book showed them brokenly and realistically. Not necessarily as always good people.<br /><br /><b>And the character development just makes me weep.</b> I like. So much. Also the slowburn of the romance was perfect and painful and ahhh. My frikkin ship.<br /><br /><b>I'm so glad I read this series!</b> And I read it all in just a few weeks which is unreasonably weird for me, who loves procrastinating series. The characters were intoxicatingly addictive and the storyline was bloody and frightening and super dark and full of broken people who were no less fierce and loving for the sourness life dealt them. I DON'T KNOW WHAT TO DO WITH MYSELF NOW. SCREAM PROBABLY. (I miss them already.)<br /><br /><br /><blockquote></blockquote>“There is no ‘this’. This is nothing.”<br />“And I am nothing,” Neil prompted. When Andrew gestured confirmation, Neil said, “And as you’ve always said, you want nothing.”<br />Andrew stared stone-faced back at him. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4516063975106700154" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1769287717?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=finished-series">finished-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=underrated">underrated</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1769287717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14782202586150320570"><i>“Fight because you don't know how to die quietly. Win because you don't know how to lose. This king's ruled long enough—it's time to tear his castle down.”</i><br/><br/><i>The King's Men</i> is one of the best books I've read in 2016, and maybe the best conclusion to a series ever - apart from Harry Potter. Nothing beats Harry Potter.<br/><br/>Honestly, though, there are so many amazing series out there. However, only a few of them have an ending that's as amazing, or even more so, as the other books in a series. Loose ends a</span>
  <span id="freeText14782202586150320570" style="display:none"><i>“Fight because you don't know how to die quietly. Win because you don't know how to lose. This king's ruled long enough—it's time to tear his castle down.”</i><br /><br /><i>The King's Men</i> is one of the best books I've read in 2016, and maybe the best conclusion to a series ever - apart from Harry Potter. Nothing beats Harry Potter.<br /><br />Honestly, though, there are so many amazing series out there. However, only a few of them have an ending that's as amazing, or even more so, as the other books in a series. Loose ends and too open or unrealistic endings happen often. Some examples are <i>Angelfall</i>, <i>Starcrossed</i> and even <i>The Raven Cycle</i>. Their last books just couldn't live up to their prequels.<br />Luckily Nora Sakavic succeded to outshine the first and second book with this conclusion. <i>The King's Men</i> had everything and more: stunning characters and character development, thrill, suspense and excitement through a plot that exceeded expectations, and most of all a worthy and satisfying ending for everyone. People got what they deserved, and I got the conclusion I wanted. Even though I endured some stabs in my very weak heart and shed a tear or three.<br /><br />This series got better with every book. It played with my patience and my hunger for more. I read the whole series in only a week. This is one of the best examples for character depth as well as female empowerment and equality.<br /><br />I cannot wait to read more from Nora Sakavic, though it might be hard to write something that can live up to <i>All for the Game</i>.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/kaispellmeier/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14782202586150320570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer346282450697384475">SO PROUD. SO PROUD OF MY PRECIOUS SONS.<br/><br/>GO NEIL! GO KEVIN! GO ANDREW! GO FOXES! Ahhh, with Kevin I feel like singing Ham's part in Dear Theodosia: "Look at my son! Pride is not the word I'm looking for!"   <span id="freeText346282450697384475" style="display:none">SO PROUD. SO PROUD OF MY PRECIOUS SONS.<br /><br />GO NEIL! GO KEVIN! GO ANDREW! GO FOXES! Ahhh, with Kevin I feel like singing Ham's part in Dear Theodosia: "Look at my son! Pride is not the word I'm looking for!" (also with Neil tbh, words can't describe how proud I am of him).<br /><br />I feel like a proud mom, is that weird? And I know I've said "proud" x1000 times in this short review, but I can't help it, THAT'S HOW I FEEL ABOUT MY FOXES. It is rare when an author makes me care so much about a whole bunch of fictional characters. I normally just love the main characters and the ocasional side character, but Nora Sakavic made me really CARE about the whole team and the coach of the team. <br /><br />At this point, if Exy was a real thing, I'd be a fan. I need Exy teams in my life.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1698086905?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=fave-couple">fave-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1698086905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4401173328417480694"><b> whAT A GOOD DAY TO THINK ABOUT ANDREIL AND HOW THEY ARE THE GREATEST THING TO HAPPEN EVER IN LITERARY HISTORY</b><br/><br/><b>ANOTHER EDIT</b>: You know how I'm always talking about how Andrew is my favourite character ever but I can never decently explain why<br/><br/>I found this on tumblr and it puts words down okay<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>Do you ever just hurt when you think about all the times Andrew must’ve taken beatings from his mother in Aaron’s stead? And how he almost killed a bunch of guys for being homophobic towards his cousin? How </blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText4401173328417480694" style="display:none"><b> whAT A GOOD DAY TO THINK ABOUT ANDREIL AND HOW THEY ARE THE GREATEST THING TO HAPPEN EVER IN LITERARY HISTORY</b><br><br><b>ANOTHER EDIT</b>: You know how I'm always talking about how Andrew is my favourite character ever but I can never decently explain why<br><br>I found this on tumblr and it puts words down okay<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>Do you ever just hurt when you think about all the times Andrew must’ve taken beatings from his mother in Aaron’s stead? And how he almost killed a bunch of guys for being homophobic towards his cousin? How Andrew would literally stab anyone if he saw a mere scratch on Kevin, if Kevin gets a simple paper cut, if a single hair on Kevin’s head is ruffled, but would voluntarily split his own knuckles open without a second thought? It hurts when I think about Andrew’s hands around Kevin’s neck, how he almost blinded himself in pursuit of Neil after he was taken away. His disregard for the terrible, terrible act that had been committed against him, the violation of his own body; while he stared deeply into his brother’s eyes, afraid of the blood he wore that wasn’t even his own. Andrew’s fiercely protective streak could be seen to be just as human as it is perceived to be inhuman because that is how he shows his concern and the warped sense of love and family that he feels towards these people. Andrew Minyard was a victim of brutal abuse and instead of victimizing himself he was only ever so stronger for it. He looked at himself and saw something that was already far beyond saving but he would do anything to keep his inner circle from a similar fate, he would take a thousand beatings if it meant that this makeshift little family he’d found himself a part of didn’t get hurt. He literally never does anything without a reason and his crap sense of morality reflects the sort of awful environment he grew up in. He has killed to protect someone that he loves and I have no doubt that he would do it again. To him, the end justified the means. It’s not a healthy or acceptable way of thinking but for Andrew it was the only way. Yes, there’s no denying he’s messed up. No, he isn’t a good person, not in the basic sense, but he’s good where it counts. And that is just one of 2036372883 reasons why he will forever be a character so very dear to my heart</blockquote>
</i><br><br>Anyway ... it's not everything I would like to say about Andrew and how proud of him I am and how he makes me cry everyday but it's something <br><br><br>---------------------<br><br><br> <i>
  <blockquote>Better then that bright future was what he already had. A court that would always be his home, a family who'd never give up on him, and Andrew, who for once hadn't wasted their time denying that this thing between them might actually mean something to both of them. <br><br>Now he couldn't help but smile, pull Andrew in. This was everything he wanted, everything he needed. And Neil was never letting go</blockquote>
</i><br><br><b>NOTES ON THE REREAD:</b><br><br>- NEIL JOSTEN IS MY BABY !!! I love him so much. I mean y'all I have NEVER seen a character verbally drag someone on the same level Neil Josten drags like HE DRAGGED RIKO STRAIGHT TO HELL FIVE TIMES IN THIS BOOK EVEN WHEN HE WAS DYING ON THE FLOOR HE COULD CALL RIKO A PIECE OF SHIT. anyway I love him so much and he deserves all the happiness in the world<br><br>- I finaLLY understand Andrew I mean I DID the first time by the end but I understand it so much more and everything makes so much sense and I will FIGHT anyone who shit talks Andrew Minyard because he has dealt with ENOUGH already w/o that and he's just I love him so much he's doing his best I'm so proud of him. <br>But no shit Andrew is such a well written, complex character and I love that Nora Sakavic didn't sacrifice his character and wrote him honestly and he's just such a good, good character I love him <br><br>- Kevin 'I've never been skiing' Day my son tbh he owns Exy so much and like he's just such a fucking dweeb when they go on holiday but he stays inside and reads history books #NERD. But anyway his whole drag and the way he OWNS the court literally daddy <br> (ok when he comes in w/ the new tattoo and he goes out playing left handed MY FAV FIGHT THEM KEVIN <b>FIGHT THEM</b>)<br><br>- Wymack is like the single least problematic person in the world he's such a good dad 2 them all and he's just such a great person how does he do it anyway tbh none of them deserve him but anyway<br><br>- DAN AND MATT ARE SO CUTE !!!! FAVE HET SHIP !!!!! THEY ARE SO GOOD IM GONNA SCREAM<br><br>- Allison: I aint getting sex. <br> Nicky: Maybe if you ask Kevin very nicely<br> "Kevin made a noise that was not human" omfg <br><br>- tbh literally just Kevin's reaction to everything. constant sigh @ the team. constant irritation @ Neil. Trying to keep tiny irresponsible children in line whilst drinking vodka like its water HONESTLY Kevin is my third fav behind Neil and Andrew but tied with Dan I love him so much<br><br>- Allison is such a queen and tbh be my irl friend<br><br>- Aaron is a piece of shit he can go die tbh the bit when he's like "ur sleeping with Andrew bc he's 'easy pray'" kys Aaron<br><br><br><br><b>TBH </b> if you're one of those people who hasn't read this trilogy yet you probably should because these book fucked me up long time !!!!!! like wyd !!!!! it's so good everything about it from the plot to the characters (mostly the characters) but serious this trilogy is easily all time fave I even rate it above the raven cycle (shocking!) its just SOO GOOD. <br><br><br><br><b>ORIGINAL REVIEW</b><br>------------------------------------------------<br> <i>"All my love to you: to the person holding this book, who took a chance on Neil and the Foxes and Exy. Thankyou for believing in something crazy with me" </i> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464746282ra/19271059.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I don't know why but I loved the authors note at the end. Maybe because I can't believe I managed to get so attached to this. I mean, a sport book?? That I'm now invested in for life ?? I can't believe I've fell in love with this much crazy <br><br>I binged read these all in like, a week, and now I'm so sad to see it all go so soon ( why don't I read slower, dammit! ) <br><br> Anyway, I guess I should talk about the actual book. -------<br><br><br>The King's Men picks up right where The Raven King left off. This is something I really like about these books - they don't have that annoying 3 chapter long reintroduction to the story at the beginning of each book that's basically filler chapters. It jumps straight back into the narrative and I love that so much. <br><br>In the third and final book of the series, things between ( literally everyone ) are heating up. I felt like the pacing here was so good. There was never a dull moment I felt like so many things were packed into these 370 pages - without it being overwhelming. The pacing in every book is fantastic, but this one managed to pack in so much genuinely good plot points, character development and fun things like games and sniping conversations between the Foxes. <br><br>I want to absolutely commend Sakavic for the movement of the plot here. All the necessary revelations and outcomes and things we wanted plot wise were finally given to us. It was so much plot and story moving, without ever dragging down the fun of the series which has always been the characters and the Exy. There is so much suspense, so many high tension scenes and so much grit. I love that these books are so dark and gritty and awful - but also fun and lights and hopeful. I love that these characters so through so many terrible, terrible ordeals and trials and tribulations but they still get up and keep going and we get to share both sides of that with them. <i>Everything</i> - the characters, the games, the overarching plots and the side plots blend so seamlessly I love it that so much is going on, without it ever being overwhelming. Everything we were waiting for happened, and it was <b>glorious</b><br><br>The series continued to be incredibly emotive to me. These are scenes and characters you really <i>feel</i> and who break your heart and make you cry and laugh and get angry. <br><br>Ah, the characters. They are truly all assholes but I say that with the absolute height of fondness in my tone. There was so much character development here for Neil, Andrew, Allison, Dan but ESPECIALLY Kevin. I loved that so much. The characters are so central and driving in this story, if their plot points and development and dynamics weren't up to scratch you'd definitely notice. But in The Kings Men they shone and I'm so glad. <br>Over 3 books I've come to know and care for all of them so much, and I'm really going to have a hard time letting them go.<br><br>These books are just outstanding, exceptional. In the way they deal with trauma, in the way they show character development both great and small (yet touching, important, monuments in it's smallness )<br><br>The writing really has impact and I felt like I was totally immersed in the story. You know when you completely forget you're lying in your bed grasping a book because really you're right there with the characters, experiencing what they do, feeling as they do, as if you're standing right beside them??<br><br>That's me with these books. <br><br>I'm going to miss these kids so much. I'm going to miss Dan fiercely objecting to anyone messing with her team. I'm going to miss Renee's quiet determination. I'm going to miss Allison's ridiculous splurge spending. I'm going to miss Matt's on-court fights. I'm going to miss Aaron's grouchiness and perpetual bad mood. I'm going to miss Nicky's loud mouth and endearing lact of tact. I'm going to miss Kevin's callous comments about no one being good enough and exasperated sighs everytime Andrew or Neil instigates a fight. I'm going to miss Wymack telling everyone to shut up. I'm going to miss Andrew's deadpan rebuffs and Neil's total inability to stop himself starting a fight. I'm going to miss Exy games and Kevin fangirling over UCR Trojans and Bee's cocoa and Sweetie's ice-cream and Roland's sly comments and the never ending bus rides.<br><br>I seriously encourage everyone to read this or at least think about it. It's hard to explain what it is exactly but trust me this is the most heartbreaking sports team you'll ever come across and everyone needs to acquaint themselves with the Palmetto State Foxes. <br><br>Never, not in a long time have I come to truly care so much for so many fictional characters. So long, my Foxes. I will miss you all! (Until the next inevitable reread anyway) <br><br>(Thank god Nora Sakavic has a blog where she's published SO MUCH extra content I need more Foxes ASAP. ) <br><br><a href="https://open.spotify.com/user/jamieson_k/playlist/5Bxvr7ugZ8CXLq6w3KrIh7" rel="nofollow noopener">my official foxhole court playlist bc I'm lame</a><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469203428ra/19792436.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="4401173328417480694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5719836571001801613"><i>Beautiful.</i><br/><br/><b>Heart wrenchingly, agonizingly <i>beautiful</i></b>. <br/><br/>You won't know what it means to be <u>happy and alive</u> until you've read this series. Honest to god it's so <b>fucking</b> amazing. <br/><br/><i><b>Andrew</b> freaking <b>Minyard</b></i>.<br/><br/><b>NEIL</b> <i>fucking</i> <b>JOSTEN</b>.<br/><br/>Leave me be. <br/>Don't mind me while I go and tattoo their names on my face. <br/><br/>JK. <br/><br/>But really tho. <br/>(<i>cries for days</i>)</span>

<div id="review_1111969090" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1111969090" />
    <a title="Lila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6659789-lila"><img alt="Lila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426228692p2/6659789.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1111969090?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lila" href="/user/show/6659789-lila">Lila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6659789-lila?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6659789-lila?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6659789-lila?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6659789-lila?shelf=mm">mm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6659789-lila?shelf=favorite-hero">favorite-hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1111969090" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16293227632637952615"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399901324ra/9607775.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>My mind is blown away.<br/>There is a special kind of rush you get when you are having final book in series in your hands. <br/>It gets even more special when that closure comes after 2 years of waiting. <br/>But this kind of emotional satisfaction I am feeling right now you get only when book is everything you hoped to be and a thousand things more. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23594461.The_King_s_Men' title='The King's Men by Nora Sakavic' rel='nofollow noopener'>The King's Men</a> was definitely worth the wait.<br/><br/>Last sentence of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18187013.The_Raven_King' title='The Raven King by Nora Sakavic' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Raven King</a> gave us pretty much a big hint where will the plot of this book go: Neil and his team</span>
  <span id="freeText16293227632637952615" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399901324ra/9607775.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My mind is blown away.<br>There is a special kind of rush you get when you are having final book in series in your hands. <br>It gets even more special when that closure comes after 2 years of waiting. <br>But this kind of emotional satisfaction I am feeling right now you get only when book is everything you hoped to be and a thousand things more. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23594461.The_King_s_Men" title="The King's Men by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The King's Men</a> was definitely worth the wait.<br><br>Last sentence of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18187013.The_Raven_King" title="The Raven King by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a> gave us pretty much a big hint where will the plot of this book go: Neil and his team will do anything to meet Ravens in championship finals. <br>But we know that's not an easy task: <br>Foxes are down to nine players and that's the the least number of players they can have in their team and be allowed to compete. <br>Team unity is still uncertain, with cousins barely tolerating upperclassmen.<br>Kevin is a very much product of his upbringing and he is scared of doing anything against his former club.<br>Andrew and Aaron's relationship was messed up even before the events in Nicky's house for Thanksgiving that led to Andrew being committed;<br>and Andrew is... well, Andrew. Nobody can predict what will Andrew do.<br>Oh, and let's not forget yakuza family who think you are misbehaved property and mobster sadistic father with penchant for blades...<br>Running is not an option anymore.<br>****<br>Ok, it all comes to this.<br>Everything we waited for, happened here, in this novel.<br><br>Stakes were already high ever since Neil joined the Foxes, but they kept getting higher and higher and I have to say that in this novel suspense was off the chart. You know how in traditional stories hero can be in all kinds of danger, but you just know he'll come unaffected because he's the hero? Nora never gave us this security blanket. When our boys were in danger, those were nail-biting, edge-of-the-seat moments and at one point I was genuinely afraid for Neil. In that way, I would say that this story dipped more into suspense genre comparing to previous, but considering the players involved, I expected nothing less than for showdown to be epic.<br>There is also a season to play and championship to win. I am still baffled that Exy is just an imaginary sport, because author paid a lot of attention on details and descriptions.<i> I'll just put my orange shirt with my gryffindor Quidditch scarf into my "sports they keep trying to persuade me are fictional" department. </i>Anyway, championship is intense and with no player to spare, Foxes get into every game like their life depends on it. Rooting for underdog will never get old and it's plot theme I will never get tired of reading.<br>But when I say that this book is everything we waited for, i didn't really mean just this. These are things we knew have to come down, but romance? I had no idea if this will even happen at some point. There was a possibility, but definitely not a promise. That's why I was never sure I can attach romance tag to series. Story was not about that and let's face it, Neil thoughts were pretty much asexual: Exy and murder-that's about it. :)<br>Well... for a little mastermind runaway expert, our boy is so completely oblivious I was enjoying watching him falling in love. I don't want to spoil it much, but it was beautiful. It was perfect. <br>It was everything.<br>The amount of love I have for Andrew is impossible to measure. I always loved damaged characters, but Andrew grabbed my heart with every scene he was in. Andrew is apathetic by default and we read so many scenes with him showing lack of interest,so when he actually does something, it's so significant, so pivotal you want to cherish it. Also, another thing I immensely respect author did with with Andrew was the fact she didn't end it with him being fixed. His issues are just too severe and deep to be healed so easily. He will never be normal, but it doesn't mean he doesn't belong anywhere.<br>I am not really sure which scene did it for me, but somewhere along the way, this story stopped being about Neil and started being about a team of nine messed up kids and their coach. We know that Foxes are ragtag bunch made of lost causes; kids everyone washed their hands off and they are team because Whymack believes they deserve another chance. In fact, Nora did this little cool countdown prompts with character's background on <a href="http://courtingmadness.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">her blog</a> and getting to know them better just cemented my feelings about Foxes.<br>I fell in love with every single one of them.<br>I cared for all of them.<br>And this why you should read this.<br>It's not really a story about Foxes trying to win championship.<br>It's not about beating Ravens or Moriyamas.<br>It's about beating the impossible odds life threw at them. And with people who love them in their team, nothing is out of reach.<br><br>Go, read this, you will not be sorry.<br><br><i>Ok, let's talk some numbers:<br>-This is third and final book in series. So, if you haven't jumped aboard Nora Sakavic ship 1)you are missing out and 2)this is not a good place to start. Go back to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17259690.The_Foxhole_Court" title="The Foxhole Court by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The Foxhole Court</a> since these books have to be read in order.<br>-With 138K+ words, this is the longest book in series.<br>-I still can't wrap my head around the fact that entire trilogy can be bought for 2$. 0_0 I would pay a lot more for quality I got from this author.<br>-Rating is pretty self-explanatory but, all the stars, guys...all the stars...</i><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16293227632637952615" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Seconds were days, were years, were the breaths that caught between their mouths and the bite of Neil's fingernails against his palms, the scrape of teeth against his lower lip and the warm slide of a tongue against his. He could feel Andrew's heartbeat thrumming against his wrists, a staccato rhythm that echoed in Neil's veins. How a man who viewed the world with such studied disconnect could kiss like this, Neil didn't know, but he wasn't going to complain.</i>

  <i>
    <blockquote> "You are a Fox. You are always going to be nothing." Andrew stubbed his cigarette out. "I hate you." <br>"Nine percent of the time you don't." <br>"Nine percent of the time I don't want to kill you. I always hate you."<br> "Every time you say that I believe you a little less." <br>"No one asked you." With that, Andrew caught Neil's face in his hands and leaned in.<br> </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I LOVE boyfriends</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer754696467328937397"><b>5+++++++stars</b><br/><br/>We got over 25k ratings and over 3k reviews for this book, nothing more to add, other than;<br/><br/>I freaking loved this series.. 🎉🎉🎉 It took me ages to get to it, but i am finally happy i got to experience this fucked up, wonderful journey. <br/><br/>Going in I had no idea what to expect, I don't know why I thought it had some supernatural elements. 🤭🤣 What i got was so much more than i expected.   <span id="freeText754696467328937397" style="display:none"><b>5+++++++stars</b><br /><br />We got over 25k ratings and over 3k reviews for this book, nothing more to add, other than;<br /><br />I freaking loved this series.. 🎉🎉🎉 It took me ages to get to it, but i am finally happy i got to experience this fucked up, wonderful journey. <br /><br />Going in I had no idea what to expect, I don't know why I thought it had some supernatural elements. 🤭🤣 What i got was so much more than i expected. A story about love, resilience, family, friendship and everything else.<br /><br />The Foxes have become family, Gaaah.. I am going to miss them. Aaaannd, this is how you write a sports story. I am now too invested in Exy. <br /><br />Neil and Andrew are the best YA/NA characters i have ever had the pleasure of reading about. Damn Nora is one talented author,too bad she doesn't have a gazillion published books. 😩 Why? Whhhhyy?<br /><br />I kept rereading and relistening to this book over and over, i didn't want it to end. <br /><br />The rest of the characters fit so well into the story and they are given time to shine. Nicky, Seth, Kevin, Dan, Matt, Allison, Renee and Coach all deserve medals. As for Aaron, the Jury will forever be out. <br /><br />The story is so engaging, Nora made mafia stuff so much fun.<br /><br />Overall, I laughed, I Gaaahd, I shed a tiny bit of a tear, I laughed so hard again, I got my heart broken, but above all, I LOVED. 😍 😍 😍<br /><br />Thank you Xia and Jan for the hand holding. 💕</span>

<div id="review_2992169132" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2992169132" />
    <a title="tappkalina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32352828-tappkalina"><img alt="tappkalina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542817471p2/32352828.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2992169132?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="tappkalina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="tappkalina" href="/user/show/32352828-tappkalina">tappkalina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781517198008" href="/book/show/29810309-the-king-s-men">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=lgbt-read">lgbt-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=favourite-couples">favourite-couples</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=7-star">7-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=favourite-characters">favourite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=friendship-family-goals">friendship-family-goals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=all-time-favourites">all-time-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=hit-close-to-home">hit-close-to-home</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32352828-tappkalina?shelf=favourite-series">favourite-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2992169132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15488545571448617776">March 14, 2020<br/><br/>If any of you watches 'Why R U the series', Andrew's "There is no 'this'" is just like Fighter's "I'M JuSt TeAsInG yOU TOr". They make me want to hit my head against the wall, but I still love them.<br/><br/>Oct 03, 2019<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>Fight because you don't know how to die quietly. Win because you don't know how to lose. This king's ruled long enough—it's time to tear his castle down.</b>
</blockquote><br/>This book deserves all the stars in the world just as the Foxes deserve all the love we can give them. <br/><br/>The first thing </span>
  <span id="freeText15488545571448617776" style="display:none">March 14, 2020<br /><br />If any of you watches 'Why R U the series', Andrew's "There is no 'this'" is just like Fighter's "I'M JuSt TeAsInG yOU TOr". They make me want to hit my head against the wall, but I still love them.<br /><br />Oct 03, 2019<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>Fight because you don't know how to die quietly. Win because you don't know how to lose. This king's ruled long enough—it's time to tear his castle down.</b>
</blockquote><br />This book deserves all the stars in the world just as the Foxes deserve all the love we can give them. <br /><br />The first thing you have to know about me is that I never binge read series. I can easily get bored of the characters and the world, but I finished this whole thing in 17 days. This is my new favourite thing in the world.<br />I love these characters with my whole heart. I haven't felt like this since the The Raven Cycle. They are so complex, so broken and so real and I want to hug them all at once. <br /><br />Also, <i>I'll have a tattoo of the paw in the first book's cover</i> soon. That's how trash I am for them. They are my family now, too. <br /><br />The second thing you have to know about me is that I usually not just don't love, but don't even like the main caharacters. But Niel Josten is my baby and I would take a bullet for him (Andrew would too, so I'm not needed here, but still). He is my all time favourite main character.<br />Maybe he never had a proper family, but Dan and Matt are the best parents he could ever have, and the Foxes are his siblings no matter what. Even Aaron, but who cares about him? Not me. And Wymack is the best grandparent. He deserves every goodness.<br />Sorry, I just love found familys, since I think family is not about blood, but people who love, accept, help and support each other.<br /><br />Now.<br />Can we take a moment to talk about Neil 'I don't swing' Josten and Andrew 'this is nothing' Minyard?<br /><br /><u>On their own they are like:</u><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I'm tired of being nothing," Neil said.</i>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Who said 'please' that made you hate the word so much?"<br />Andrew gazed at him in silence for a minute. "I did."</i>
</blockquote><br /><u>Together:</u><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I've never belonged anywhere or had the right to call anything my own. But Coach gave me keys to the court, and you told me to stay. You gave me a key and called it home." Neil clenched his hand, imagining the bite of metal against his palm, and lifted his gaze to Andrew's face. "I haven't had a home since my parents died."</i>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I didn't say anything then because I knew I'd look out for only me when the world went to hell. I don't want to be that person anymore. I want to go back for you."</i>
</blockquote><br />I LOVE the constant ask for consent between them, but at the same time my heart breaks every time.<br /><b>
  <blockquote>"Yes or no?" Andrew asked.<br />"Yes," Neil said.</blockquote>
</b><br />They do it in this way, waiting for a proper, clear answer because of the horrible, traumatic things happened to them in the past. Andrew couldn't say no (or if he did, it was no use) to different types of abuse, and Niel couldn't touch his father while he beat him, so they understand each other's boundaries. That's why they work.<br /><br />And the trust:<br /><blockquote>"You're wrong," Nathaniel said. "They can't leave without Andrew, and Andrew won't go anywhere until he talks to me."</blockquote><br />And my Foxes:<br /><b>
  <blockquote>"You can't have him," Nicky said. "He belongs with us."</blockquote>
</b><br /><b>Finally:</b><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Better than that bright future was what he already had: a court that would always be home, a family who'd never give up on him, and Andrew, who for once hadn't wasted their time denying that this thing between them might actually mean something to both of them.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />All in all, this book has just reminded me of why do I love reading in the first place and I will be grateful for that forever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15488545571448617776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1828294348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6969760031137602685"><i> "Neil had been doing one stupid thing after another all year long and this had turned into the best year of his life." </i> <br/><br/><b> THIS. SERIES. HAS. RUINED. ME. </b> I haven't read a series in a long time that I was so emotionally invested like how I was with this one. I honestly wasn't expecting to like this story, let alone be so obsessed with it the way I am now. This series took me by storm, and I am glad to have ended my year (ehh, it's close enough to say that) with this series.<br/><br/>I loved how Sakavic wro</span>
  <span id="freeText6969760031137602685" style="display:none"><i> "Neil had been doing one stupid thing after another all year long and this had turned into the best year of his life." </i> <br /><br /><b> THIS. SERIES. HAS. RUINED. ME. </b> I haven't read a series in a long time that I was so emotionally invested like how I was with this one. I honestly wasn't expecting to like this story, let alone be so obsessed with it the way I am now. This series took me by storm, and I am glad to have ended my year (ehh, it's close enough to say that) with this series.<br /><br />I loved how Sakavic wrote these characters. I loved how she messed with your emotions. I loved how I was on the edge of my seat in most of the book. I loved how it ended. I just loved <b> every.single.thing. </b> So, thank you Nora Sakavic for making me a complete mess over the past week. <br /><br />I cried. I laughed. I cried some more. And I smiled. So, once again, thank you Nora Sakavic for this amazing series. This series will be with me for a long time, and I will never forget these characters.<br /><br />If you haven't read this series, you need to. It's one of the best series I have read in a long time. This series deserves all the hype it has.<br /><br /><i> "He'd come to the Foxhole Court every inch a lie, but his friends made him into someone real." </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6969760031137602685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2494360143" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2494360143" />
    <a title="Optimist ♰King&#39;s Wench♰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench"><img alt="Optimist ♰King&#39;s Wench♰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580443293p2/12766897.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2494360143?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Optimist ♰King&#39;s Wench♰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Optimist ♰King&#39;s Wench♰" href="/user/show/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench">Optimist ♰King&#39;s Wench♰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=boys-who-like-boys">boys-who-like-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=torture">torture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=source-amazon-audible">source-amazon-audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=boo-yah-straight-butter-baby">boo-yah-straight-butter-baby</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=favorites-2018">favorites-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12766897-optimist-king-s-wench?shelf=haters">haters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2494360143" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17788186521633998353"><b>Re-listen 2/2019</b><br/><br/>Hello. My name is Cupcake and I'm a Foxes addict.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549602997ra/27032269.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It's confirmed since I legit just power listened to <b>12 hrs, 33 mins</b> of this book. Despite the so so narration the story itself is so captivating that it almost made it a non-issue. <i>Almost.</i> If I didn't love this series so much I probably wouldn't be so passionate about the narration, but these characters deserved someone phenomenal rather than mediocre.<br/><br/>I probably won't listen to it again in the future but it was still nice hanging o</span>
  <span id="freeText17788186521633998353" style="display:none"><b>Re-listen 2/2019</b><br><br>Hello. My name is Cupcake and I'm a Foxes addict.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549602997ra/27032269.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's confirmed since I legit just power listened to <b>12 hrs, 33 mins</b> of this book. Despite the so so narration the story itself is so captivating that it almost made it a non-issue. <i>Almost.</i> If I didn't love this series so much I probably wouldn't be so passionate about the narration, but these characters deserved someone phenomenal rather than mediocre.<br><br>I probably won't listen to it again in the future but it was still nice hanging out with the Foxes again and getting caught up in their story all over again.<br><br>And now I'm verklempt all over again that it's over again.<br><br><b>🐾🐾🐾🐾🐾🐾REVIEW OF THE ENTIRE SERIES🐾🐾🐾🐾🐾🐾</b> <br><br>Undoubtedly superlatives will fail me in this review. Thankfully, there are eleventy-seven lazillion other reviews so I will <i>try</i> to keep this short. Try, being the operative word.<br><br>I would say I loved this series but considering it has consumed my life for the past several days, robbed me of sleep and occupied my thoughts, "loved" feels insufficient. <b>It became my obsession.</b> <br><br>For anyone who hasn't read it, I do believe this originally was one big fic that due to its whopping size (clocks in at just over 1200 pgs) was broken up into 3 books for publication. I say this because <b>I believe it was meant to be read as one story. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17259690.The_Foxhole_Court__All_for_the_Game___1_" title="The Foxhole Court (All for the Game, #1) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The Foxhole Court</a> isn't meant to be read as a standalone</b>. It will likely leave you wanting due to some horrific shenanigans that occur amongst the Foxes. I'm not ever going to condone the events but somewhere during <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18187013.The_Raven_King__All_for_the_Game___2_" title="The Raven King (All for the Game, #2) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a> I <b>understood</b> why they did what they did. Nevertheless, it is 1/3 of the story and only reading it is a disservice to the story arc as a whole.<br><br>Primarily because Neil's first love is Exy and through Exy he's introduced to the other great love of his life, so if you're a romance reader like me you gotta stick it out. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17259690.The_Foxhole_Court__All_for_the_Game___1_" title="The Foxhole Court (All for the Game, #1) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The Foxhole Court</a> illustrates his undying passion for the game to perfection. He fell in love with Exy as a boy. Circumstances of his life stripped it from him and then through a series of events gave it back. In a vain effort to give his life some meaning after he's lost everything he lets himself have Exy again as a high school senior at a small school in Millport, Arizona.<br><br>He never in a million years thought his play at a an unfamiliar position as a walk on would put him on Palmetto State University's radar. But it did.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534721636i/26158787._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>David Wymack, coach of the Foxes, and his team have some rather unorthodox recruitment tactics but they succeed in signing their new striker and getting him to South Carolina in the end. <br><br><b>While Neil reacquaints himself with his love of Exy, I fell in love with Neil.</b> Trust me, no one was more surprised by this development with a character like Andrew hanging around but it's true. Neil has lived through hell, literally, and somehow someway he's retained a fundamental kindness and selflessness. He's the most resilient character I can remember ever reading about. He's not going to quit. Not ever. Exy's the only thing that's ever given him anything back and he's going to give it his all until he's got nothing left. A gamer through and through and that sort of passion has a way of galvanizing a team. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534721636i/26158788._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He brought tears to my eyes with his devotion and loyalty to the Foxes. He will sacrifice himself time and time again for them. Course his mouth puts them in the crosshairs more than once but I loved that he wasn't going to let his fear stop him from protecting them or stand in the way of his dream. <br><br>His passion and drive make them more of a cohesive unit than they've ever been which makes their small, rag tag team that's been ignored and discounted by <b>everyone</b> more dangerous than anyone could've foreseen. It also nets Neil something he's never had before: a family. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534721636i/26158789._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That hit two of my most treasured reading experiences: making a family and team unity. <br><br><b><i>All for the Game</i> is heavily weighted in sport.</b> If you are a sports fan and this book doesn't get your adrenaline pumping... I... *shrugs* I don't even know what to say. As a huge sports fan, I'm not embarrassed to say that a couple games made me verklempt. It's the classic tale of David vs. Goliath. They're outnumbered. They're inexperienced. But they've got heart, grit and determination. <b>And they've got each other.</b><br><br>Exy has brought these people together but they also share a checkered and varying degrees of horrific pasts which makes them connecting with one other (at times) challenging. Neil is very intelligent but he's also oblivious when it comes to recognizing other's actions for what they are. So it's left to the reader to decipher and decode those actions through Neil's self-abasing prism. <br><br>There isn't a lot of <b>
  <i>overt</i>
</b> romance. Neil sees his future as a finite entity and everything in his life up to now has been evanescent, as is life on the run. But as he finds his place amongst the Foxes you can see hope flicker to life. He begins to trust them and finds himself increasingly drawn to another.<br><br>These two are unquestionably soulmates but they have absolutely no idea how traditional romantic relationships work nor, I suspect, would they be interested in engaging in that sort of squishy marshmallowness. Truthfully, they would be nowhere near as interesting if they were. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>He didn't know what this thing between them was anymore. He didn't know what he wanted or needed it to be. He just knew he had to hold on for as long as he could.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>There is very little sex content (lots of kissing and one oral scene that's not titillating) but there is a <u>WHOLE LOT OF VIOLENCE</u>. Be forewarned. The bad wrong starts in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17259690.The_Foxhole_Court__All_for_the_Game___1_" title="The Foxhole Court (All for the Game, #1) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The Foxhole Court</a>, gets worse in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18187013.The_Raven_King__All_for_the_Game___2_" title="The Raven King (All for the Game, #2) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a> and made me MURDEROUS! With the dramatic conclusion occurring in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23594461.The_King_s_Men__All_for_the_Game___3_" title="The King's Men (All for the Game, #3) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The King's Men</a> which made my skin crawl. I'll just say, it wasn't anywhere near bloody enough for my tastes. But I am a vengeful bitch. <br><br>Fear not, it does end happily for more than just the primary couple. I don't think it's possible to read this and not become invested in all of these characters. They are all layered and complex and have surprises up their sleeves.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534721636i/26158790._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Is this series perfect? Nope. It could've been paired down, it's sometimes redundant, the game of Exy is a fictional one but the rules of the game weren't given until <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18187013.The_Raven_King__All_for_the_Game___2_" title="The Raven King (All for the Game, #2) by Nora Sakavic" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a>. I don't know how the NCAA wouldn't have cracked down on the Ravens antics long ago nor can I fathom how these players could perform optimally after the way they treat their bodies <b>(trigger warning for drug usage)</b>. Some of the events are far-fetched, outlandish even and one thing in Neil's backstory just doesn't not add up for me.<br><br>But I'll tell you what, it's says something to me if a story can sink its teeth into me like this one has and <i>that</i> is something I can't discount. Not only could I not put it down, but... I can't even believe I'm about to say this after 1200+ pgs, but I'm sad it's over and I wish there were more. #certifiable <br><br>So I'll be burning an audible credit soon (possibly three depending on how the first one goes) so I can re-experience this once more when it releases. Here's hoping the narrator doesn't fuck it up.<br><br>Believe the hype. 13K+ ratings/reviews and an average of over 4 stars isn't a lie.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17788186521633998353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1788966989" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1788966989" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56662187-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539790744p2/56662187.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1788966989?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/56662187-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1788966989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12499571503123305453">Rereading these books made me appreciate them even more. Especially this last one. These characters are so complex that spending more time with them can only make me love them more. <br/><br/>I could rant for pages about The Foxes and what Nora Sakavic did with these books. On of the things I appreciate most is how she was brave enough to take the triggers and topics that make people squeamish and address them head on. It's not for effect or to add some angst in. She shows how people live the best they ca</span>
  <span id="freeText12499571503123305453" style="display:none">Rereading these books made me appreciate them even more. Especially this last one. These characters are so complex that spending more time with them can only make me love them more. <br /><br />I could rant for pages about The Foxes and what Nora Sakavic did with these books. On of the things I appreciate most is how she was brave enough to take the triggers and topics that make people squeamish and address them head on. It's not for effect or to add some angst in. She shows how people live the best they can when faced with impossible difficulties. These characters are so flawed, but they're also some of the strongest characters. <br /><br />Spoilers<br />-<br />-<br />-<br />-<br /><br /><br />She also stresses again and again verbal consent in a way I have never seen in a YA book (or any book for that matter?). She understands how people's minds process trauma and how it affects their relationships. I noticed a lot more this time around how Neil is the only one who understands Andrew. It's the reason they work despite everything Andrew has endured because Neil stops when Andrew says no, and he understands without Andrew having to explain himself. (which Andrew never explains himself.)<br /><br />The first time reading these books, I was really focussed on Neil and Andrew. This time Kevin drew my eye a lot. His development in the last book was incredible. I saw it the first time, but this reread it hit me in the gut. Kevin never had the spine to stand up for himself after all the abuse, but watching Neil for the last few months, he decided to try. When he got his tattoo changed, I wanted to cheer. When he talked to the press about Wymack and Riko, all bravado and strong words, I realized just how far he'd come. I loved seeing that, and Kevin became just as much a favorite as Neil and Andrew. <br /><br />These characters will continue to occupy my thoughts for a very very long time. They make me laugh (looking at you Nicky Hemmick), and make me sob (that's you Andreil). I'm really grateful for these books and the impact they have had on me. Favorite trilogy ever that's for sure. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12499571503123305453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1656107538" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1656107538" />
    <a title="Simone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16882244-simone"><img alt="Simone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531247180p2/16882244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1656107538?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simone" href="/user/show/16882244-simone">Simone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23667559-the-king-s-men">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16882244-simone?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16882244-simone?shelf=athletes-sports">athletes-sports</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16882244-simone?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16882244-simone?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16882244-simone?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1656107538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15782462940609384195"><b>'Reread' via audiobook December 2018:<br/><br/>WafrEocLmEJkeIOerknMiofElaeA = !!!<br/><br/>^^^That's me resting my case here: perfect narration for a perfect book/series!</b> ❤️<br/>----------------------------------------------<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“Stay,” Andrew said, and leaned down to kiss him.<br/>Time was nothing. Seconds were days, were years, were the breaths that caught between their mouths and the bite of Neil's fingernails against his palms, the scrape of teeth against his lower lip and the warm slide of a tongue against his. He could f</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText15782462940609384195" style="display:none"><b>'Reread' via audiobook December 2018:<br><br>WafrEocLmEJkeIOerknMiofElaeA = !!!<br><br>^^^That's me resting my case here: perfect narration for a perfect book/series!</b> ❤️<br>----------------------------------------------<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Stay,” Andrew said, and leaned down to kiss him.<br>Time was nothing. Seconds were days, were years, were the breaths that caught between their mouths and the bite of Neil's fingernails against his palms, the scrape of teeth against his lower lip and the warm slide of a tongue against his. He could feel Andrew's heartbeat thrumming against his wrists, a staccato rhythm that echoed in Neil's veins. How a man who viewed the world with such studied disconnect could kiss like this, Neil didn't know, but he wasn't going to complain.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>The romance between Neil and Andrew is probably the slowest slow burn in the history of slow burns, but I loved every goddamn minute of their – how did Neil call it? - oh, yes, not-relationship! ;-)<br><br>Oh, God! It is really hard for me to say good-bye to the team, especially to Neil and Andrew, who are so dear to my heart and I can tell you without lying that they are still in my head, even if I have finished this book a day ago. Be warned that this will be more of a rambling than a decent review because my feelings are still all over the place. <br><br>In my review of The Raven King I said I was seeking for revenge, revenge for the things Riko did to Neil aaaaand...<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431693882ra/14860428.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>I got it! ;-)<br><br>On the court...<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473010394ra/20385558.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>(Thank goodness not this time! Finally – <i>finally!</i> - the team did not only <i>act</i> like a team, it <i>was</i> a team! The path was not only rocky, there were holes the size of the whole Foxhole Court, but after being back to square one at the beginning of this book, what they achieved on the court spoke volumes of how far they have come with all their problems and differences.) <br><br>… but also aside of it. Yes, Andrew! Yes, I heard you saying 'revenge is a motivator only for the weak-willed'! I've said the boys are still in my head, right? ;-) So let's say I got justice. At what cost? Phew, for a moment I almost felt bad for Riko. Um, no... scratch that! That would be a lie! But believe me when I say that you don't want to mess with the mafia!<br><br>Speaking of mafia... In case you haven't read this book yet: remember the 58% mark! You should stock up on whatever makes you happy because you will need it. That's when Neil's past caught up with him and it almost killed me. I guess, you know the feeling when you cannot read fast enough to see if everything is going to be okay, but at the same time you dread to turn the page because you are really terrified of what is going to happen next? Yep, this was one of those situations...<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473010394i/20385559.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br>If I could marry a book character this would be Coach Wymack. He made me laugh so hard with his sarcasm and his dry comments, but I also loved his way of handling the boys and girls and his devotion to the team, like a mother lion defending her cubs.<br><br>But what I loved the most were Andrew and Neil and their character development.<br><br>Andrew...<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473010394i/20385560.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>with his sociopathic tendencies, his protective streak of everyone he decided to protect (even if his methods were more than twisted and questionable sometimes), but most of all that he allowed Neil to come near, despite of his experiences during his awful childhood.<br><br>And Neil...<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473010394i/20385561.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>who refuses to give in to anything that threatens to compromise all he ever wanted.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Better than that bright future was what he already had: a court that would always be home, a family who'd never give up on him, and Andrew, who for once hadn't wasted their time denying that this thing between them might actually mean something to both of them.<br><br>This was everything he wanted, everything he needed, and Neil was never letting go.</i>
</blockquote><br><i>This review has been posted on <a href="https://dirtybooksobsessiongroup.wordpress.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Dirty Books Obsession</a> </i></span>
